For hands-free operation just say \"Hey Cortana Control Home\" followed by a command phrase like \"turn on the master bedroom light.\"  Following a successful command, Cortana reads back exactly what your Premise server did, so you know for sure what task was performed.\r\n\r\nThe additional required software Premise Home Control and my Premise SpeechParser module are completely FREE, plus I show step by step videos on how to set everything up on my YouTube channel (see app support link).\r\n\r\nINSTALLATION:\r\nThis app requires that you have a working Premise Home Control server setup already, and it also requires that SpeechPraser be installed on the Premise server.  If you are new to home automation, please see the tutorial videos on my YouTube channel (use app support link) for how to setup the Premise server and the SpeechParser module.\r\n\r\nThis app is meant to be installed on a device other than your Premise server.  This device must be compatible with Windows Universal Apps (e.g. Windows 10 or Windows Phone 8.1 or higher). \r\n\r\nOpen the Cortana Control Home app, and fill in your Premise server address, port, username and password.  Click \"Set Values\" and close the app.  The app itself is just a front end to input the server values.  A background server does all the work by receiving the spoken phrase from Cortana, and then providing Cortana a sentence to read back.\r\n\r\nSince the app uses an HTTP connection, it means sensitive home automation commands will not be encrypted (see warranty section under Additional Terms for more information).\r\n\r\nThis app will send a text string representing what was spoken to your Premise server.  Your Premise Home Control server does all the processing via my SpeechParser module (download for free from my YouTube channel).  The SpeechParser command phrases are easily customized, and are NOT order dependent. Different religious groups include different books within their canons, in different orders, and sometimes divide or combine books, or incorporate additional material into canonical books.\r\n\r\nThe Hebrew Bible, or Tanakh, contains twenty-four books divided into three parts: the five books of the Torah (\"teaching\" or \"law\"), the Nevi'im (\"prophets\"), and the Ketuvim (\"writings\").\r\n\r\nChristian Bibles range from the sixty-six books of the Protestant canon to the eighty-one books of the Ethiopian Orthodox Church canon. The first part of Christian Bibles is the Old Testament, which contains, at minimum, the twenty-four books of the Hebrew Bible divided into thirty-nine books and ordered differently than the Hebrew Bible. The Catholic Church and Eastern Christian churches also hold certain deuterocanonical books and passages to be part of the Old Testament canon. The second part is the New Testament, containing twenty-seven books: the four Canonical gospels, Acts of the Apostles, twenty-one Epistles or letters, and the Book of Revelation.\r\n\r\nBy the 2nd century BCE Jewish groups had called the Bible books \"holy,\" and Christians now commonly call the Old and New Testaments of the Christian Bible \"The Holy Bible\" (τὰ βιβλία τὰ ἅγια, tà biblía tà ágia) or \"the Holy Scriptures\" (η Αγία Γραφή, e Agía Graphḗ).
